 off ; and nought else anigh she , save the bird in the brake , or 
 fly on their errand eagerly from place to place . then , as it 
 be , without she will be tell they , her limb and her foot turn 
 she about to the shore where lie the Sending Boat , and she go 
 speedily but quietly thitherward , her heart beat quick , for fear 
 lest something should yet stay she , and her eye glance from brake 
 to bush , as if she look to see some enemy , old or new , come out 
 thence . 

 so now she will be clear enough to her foot , and they bring she 
 down to the water - side and the long strand , past which the wide water 
 lie windless and gleam in the hot afternoon . then lightly she 
 step aboard , and awake the Sending Boat with blood - offering , and 
 it obey she , and speed swiftly on the way to the southward . 



 CHAPTER X. birdalone come to the isle of the QUEENS 



 birdalone awake the next morning while the boat be yet speed over 
 the water , and the sun be up : but she be hard on the land , which 
 sit low and green , like a meadow exceed fair , on the bosom of the 
 water , and many goodly tree be sprinkle about the greenland . but 
 from amidst the tree , no great way from the water 's edge , rise a 
 great house , white and fair , as if it be new - builded , and all 
 glorious with pinnacle , and tabernacle set with imagery . 

 presently the boat 's bow run into the reed and rush at the brim of 
 the water , and Birdalone step ashore without more ado , and the 
 scent of the meadow - sweet amongst which she land bring back unto 
 she the image of Green Eyot that while agone . 

 but now when she be ashore the dread take hold of she again , and her 
 knee tremble under she , so that she might scarce stand , so fearful 
 be she of walk into some trap ; especially when she behold that 
 goodly house , lest therein await she some proud and cruel lady , and 
 no kind damsel to deliver she . 

 she look about she , and see in all the fair meadow neither man nor 
 woman , nor draught - beast nor milch - beast , nought but the little 
 creature of the brake and the bent - grass , which be but as the 
 blossom thereof ; and the bird run in the herbage or singing 
 amidst the tree - bough . 

 then she think that she must need go forward , or belike her errand 
 would not speed ; that the Sending Boat might not obey she , unless she 
 see through the adventure to the end ; so she go on toward the house 
 quaking . 

 soon be she at the porch of the white palace , and have see no man 
 nor hear any voice of man ; much she marvel , despite her dread , at 
 the beauty of the said house , and the newness thereof ; for it be as 
 one flower arise out of the earth , and every part of it make the 
 beauty of the other part more excellent ; and so new it be , that it 
 would have seem as if the mason thereof have but strike their 
 scaffold yesterday , save that under the very foot of the wall the 
 sweet garden flower grow all uncrushe . 

 now come Birdalone through the porch unto the screen of the great 
 hall ; and she stop a little to recover her breath , that she might 
 be the quieter and calm amongst the great folk and mighty whom she 
 look to find therein . so she gather heart ; but one thing daunt 
 she , to wit , that she hear no sound come from that great and goodly 
 hall , so that she doubt if it be perchance leave desert by they 
 who have be its lord . 

 she raise her hand to the door of the screen , and it open easily 
 before she , and she enter , and there indeed she see new tiding . 
 for the board end - long and over - thwart be set , and thereat be 
 sit a many folk , and their hand be reach out to knife and to 
 dish , and to platter and cup ; but such a hush there be within , that 
 the song of the garden bird without sound to she as loud as they 
 be the voice of the child of Adam . 

 next she see that all that company , from the great folk on the dais 
 down to those who stand about the hall to do the service , be woman , 
 one and all ; not one carle might she see from where she stand : 
 lovely be they many of they , and none less than comely ; their 
 cheek be bright , and their eye gleam , and their hair flow 
 down fair of fashion . and she stand , and durst not move a long 
 while , but expect when someone would speak a word , and all should 
 turn their head toward the new - comer . but none move nor spake . 
 and the fear increase in she amidst that hush , and weigh so heavy 
 on her heart , that at last she might endure it no long , but fall 
 swoon to the floor . 

 when she come to herself ; and the swoon - dream have leave she , she see 
 by the changing of the sun through the hall - window , that she have 
 lain there long , more nearly two hour than one ; and at first she 
 cover her face with her hand as she crouch there , that she might 
 not see the sight of the silent hall , for yet be it as hush as 
 before . then slowly she arise , and the sound of her raiment and her 
 stir foot be loud in her ear . but when she be upright on her 
 foot , she harden her heart , and go forth into the hall , and no 
 less be her wonder than erst . for when she come close to those 
 lady as they sit at table , and her raiment brush the raiment of 
 the serve - woman as she pass by , then see she how no breath come 
 from any of these , and that they neither spake nor move , because 
 they be dead . 

 at first , then , she think to flee away at once , but again she have 
 mind of her errand , and so go up the hall , and so forth on to the 
 dais ; and there again , close by the high table , she see new tiding . 
 for there be set a bi , cover with gold and pall , and on it be 
 lay a tall man , a king , belt and crown ; and beside the said 
 bi , by the head of the king , kneel a queen of exceed goodly 
 body , clothe all in raiment of pearl and bawdekin ; and her hand be 
 clasp together , and her mouth be draw , and her brow knit with the 
 anguish of her grief . but athwart the king 's breast lie a naked 
 sword all bloody ; and this birdalone note , that whereas the lady be 
 of skin and hue as if she be alive , the king be yellow as wax , and 
 his cheek be shrink , and his eye have be close by the waker 
 of the dead . 

 Long Birdalone look and wonder ; and now if her fear be less , 
 her sorrow be more for all that folk sit there dead in their 
 ancient state and pomp . and be not the thought clean out of her 
 head , that yet they might awake and challenge she , and that she might 
 be make one of that silent company . Withal she feel her head 
 begin to fail she , and she fear that she might swoon again and 
 never waken more , but lie for ever beside that image of the dead 
 king . 

 so then she refrain she both of fear and sorrow , and walk 
 speedily down the hall , look neither to the right nor left : and 
 she come forth into the pleasance , but stay there nought , so nigh 
 it seem to that hush company . Thence come she forth into the 
 open meadow , and sweet and dear seem its hot sunshine and noisy 
 bird and rustle leaf . nevertheless , so great be the tumult of 
 her spirit , that once more she grow faint , and feel that she might 
 scarce go far . so she drag herself into the shade of a thorn- 
 tree , and let her body sink unto the ground , and lie there long 
 unwitting . 



 CHAPTER XI . and now she come to the isle of the king 



 when Birdalone come to herself it be draw toward the glooming , 
 and she rise up hastily , and go down to the Sending Boat , for she 
 would not for aught abide the night in that fearful isle , lest the 
 flock of the hall should come alive and walk in the dusk and the 
 dark . she step aboard lightly , and yield her blood to the pride 
 of that ferry , and it awake and bear her forth , and she go through 
 the night till she fall asleep . 

 when she awake it be broad day and the sun just arise , and lo ! 
 before she , some half mile off , an isle rugge and rocky , and go 
 up steep from the shore ; and then , hold as it be by the fang of 
 the rock and pike of the high land , be a castle , white , high , 
 and hugely build , though , because of the rock - land belike , it 
 spread not much abroad . like to the lovely house of yesterday , it 
 seem new - builded ; and , little as Birdalone know of such matter , 
 her heart tell she that this new house be fashion for battle . 

 she be downcast when she see the isle so rugged and forbidding , but 
 when the boat come aland in a stony bight , whence the ground go up 
 somewhat steeply toward the height , she go ashore straightway , and 
 toil up toward the white battlement . presently she find herself 
 in a strait and rugged path betwixt two wall of rock , so that she 
 lose sight of the castle a while , till she come out on to a level 
 place which look down from aloft on to the blue water , but all over 
 against her close at hand be the great tower and wall . she be 
 wear by the rough road , and over helpless she feel she , and all too 
 little to deal with that huge morsel of the world ; and her valiancy 
 give way , and her trust in her errand . she sit down on a stone and 
 weep abundantly . 

 after a while she be amend , and she look up and see the huge 
 hold , and say : Yea , but if it be less by the half than it be , it 
 would still be big enough to cow I . yet she stand not up . then she 
 put forth a foot of she , and say aloud : sorely hath this rough road 
 try Atra 's shoon and their goodly window - work ; if they be to be 
 know I must be speedy on my journey or go barefoot . 

 as she speak she stand up , and the sound of her own voice fright 
 she , though nought noiseless be the place ; for the wind be there , 
 and beat to and fro the castle and the rock , and run baffle into 
 every corner of that market - place of nothing . for in that garth be 
 neither knight nor squire nor sergeant ; no spear - head glitter from 
 the wall , no gleam of helm show from the war - swale ; no porter be 
 at the gate ; the drawbridge over the deep ghyll be down , the 
 portculli be up , and the great door cast wide open . 

 birdalone steel her heart and go forward swiftly , and over the 
 bridge , and enter the basecourt , and come without more ado to the 
 door of the great hall , and open it easily , as with the door of 
 yesterday , look to find another show like unto that one ; and even 
 so it fall out . 

 Forsooth the hall be nought light and lovely , and gay with gold and 
 bright colour , as that other , but beset with huge round pillar that 
 bore aloft a wide vault of stone , and of stone be the table ; and 
 the halling that hang on the wall be terrible picture of battle 
 and death , and the fall of city , and tower a - tumble and house 
 a - flaming . 

 none the less there also be the shape of folk that move not nor 
 spake , though not so thronged be that hall as the other one ; and it 
 seem as if man be sit there at a council rather than a feast . 
 close by Birdalone 's right hand as she enter be stand in a row 
 along the screen big man - at - arm all weapone , and their face hide 
 by their sallet ; and down below the dai on either side of the high 
 table be again a throng of all - arm man ; and at the high - table 
 itself ; and look down the hall , sit three crown king , each with 
 his draw sword lie across his knee , and three long - hoary wise man 
 stand before they at the nether side of the board . 

 birdalone look on it all , strive with her fear : but yet more 
 there be , for she deem that need must she go through the hall up 
 to the dai , lest the Sending Boat deny its obedience . up toward the 
 dais she go then , pass by weapone man who sit as if abide the 
 council 's end at the end - long table . and now , though no shape of 
 man there spake or breathe , yet sound lack not ; for within the 
 hall go the wind as without , and beat about from wall to wall , and 
 drave clang and clash from the weapon hang up , and wave the arra , 
 and fare moaning in the nook , and hum in the vault above . 

 come she up to the dais then , and stand beside one of the wise man , 
 and look on the king , and see the mightiness which have be in 
 they , and quake before they . then she turn from they and look 
 down to the floor , and lo ! there , just below the dai , lie a woman on 
 a golden bier ; exceed fair have she be , with long yellow hair 
 stream down from her head ; but now waxen white she be , with ashen 
 lip and sunken cheek . Clad be she in raiment of purple and pall , 
 but the bosom of she be bar on one side , and therein be the road 
 whereby the steel have fare which have be her bane . 

 now when Birdalone have gaze thereon a while , she deem that if she 
 tarry there long amidst those fierce man by the dead woman , she 
 should lose her wit full soon , so sore the fear , hold back , beset she 
 now . wherefore she turn and go hastily down the hall , and out - a- 
 door , and over the bridge , and run fleet - foot down the rocky way 
 whereby she have come , till she could run no far , and lie down 
 under a great stone breathless and fordone ; yet her heart uphold she 
 and suffer she not to swoon , belike because she have give her limb 
 such hard work to do . 

 there she lie awake and trouble for an hour or more , and then she 
 fall asleep , and sleep till the day be wear toward sunset , and 
 nought meddle with she . she arise and go to her ship somewhat 
 downhearte , wonder how many such terror should befall she ; nay , 
 whether the Sending Boat would so lead she that henceforth she should 
 happen on no child of Adam but such as be dead image of the 
 living . have all the world die since she leave the Isle of the Young 
 and the Old ? 

 Howsoever , she have nought to do save to board her ferry , and content 
 its greedy soul with her blood , and drive it with the spell - word . 
 and thereafter , when it be speed on , and the twilight dusk 
 apace , she look aback , and seem to see the far - off woodland in 
 the northern ort , and the oak - clothe ridge , where she have meet her wood- 
 mother ; and then it be as if Habundia be say to she : Meet 
 again we shall . and therewith straightway become life sweet unto 
 she . 

 deepen then the dusk , and become night , and she float on through 
 it , and be asleep alone on the bosom of the water . 



 CHAPTER XII . of BIRDALONE , how she come unto the isle of nothing 



 long before sunrise , in the very morn - dusk , she awake and find that 
 her ferry have take land again . little might she see what the say 
 land be like ; so she sit patiently and abode the day in the boat ; 
 but when day be come , little more be to see than erst . for flat 
 be the isle , and scarce raise above the wash of the leeward ripple 
 on a fair day ; nor be it either timbere or bushed or grass , and , 
 so far as Birdalone might see , no one foot of it differ in aught 
 from another . Natheless she deem that she be bind to go ashore 
 and seek out the adventure , or spoil her errand else . 

 out of the boat she step then , and find the earth all pave of a 
 middling gravel , and nought at all grow there , not even the 
 small of herb ; and she stoop down and search the gravel , and 
 find neither worm nor beetle therein , nay nor any one of the sharp 
 and slimy creature which be will not in such ground . 

 a little far she go , and yet a little far , and no change 
 there be in the land ; and yet she go on and find nothing ; and she 
 wend her way southward by the sun , and the day be windless . 

 at last she have go a long way and have no sight of water south of 
 the isle , nor have she see any hill , nay , not so much as an ant - heap , 
 whence she might look far around ; and it seem to she that she 
 might go on for ever , and reach the heart of Nowhither at last . 
 wherefore she think she would turn back and depart this ugly isle , 
 and that no other adventure abide she therein . and by now it be 
 high noon ; and she turn about and take a few step on the backward 
 road . 

 but even therewith it seem as if the sun , which heretofore have be 
 shin brightly in the heaven , go out as a burn - down candle , and 
 all be become dull grey over head , as all under foot be a dull dun . 
 but Birdalone deem she could follow a straight course back again , 
 and so walk on sturdily . hour after hour she go and stay not , 
 but see before her no glimpse of the northern shore , and no change in 
 the aspect of the ground about she . 

 it have so happen that a little before she have turn to go back , 
 she have eat her dinner of a piece of bread and a morsel of cheese , 
 and now as she stoop and peer on the ground , look for some 
 sign of the way , as her foot - print go south , and have her eye low 
 anigh the earth , she see something white at her foot in the gathering 
 dusk   for the day be wear , and she put her hand to it and lift 
 it , and find it a crumb of bread , and know that it must have come 
 from her dinner of ' seven hour ago , whereas till that time her bread 
 have lie unbroken in her scrip . fear and anguish smite she 
 therewith , for she see that in that dull land , every piece whereof 
 be like every other piece , she must have go about in a ring , and 
 come back again to where she first turn to make for the northern 
 shore . 

 yet would she not cast aside all hope , but clothe herself in her 
 valiancy . Forsooth she know it avail nought to try to move on in 
 the twilight ; so she lay herself down on that waste , and make up her 
 mind to sleep if she might , and abide the new day there , and then to 
 strive with the way once more , for belike , she think , it may be 
 fair to - morrow , and the sun shin . and as she be very weary with 
 tramp the waste all day , she fall asleep at once , and sleep the 
 short night through . 

 but when she awake , and see what the new day be , her heart fall 
 indeed , for now be she encompass and shut in with a thick dark 
 mist   though it seem to be broad day , so that have there be aught 
 to see she would not have see it her own length away from she . so 
 there she stand , hang her head , and strive to think ; but the 
 master - thought of death draw nigh scatter all other thought , or 
 make they dim and feeble . 

 long she stand there ; but suddenly something come into her mind . she 
 set her hand to the fair - broider pouch which hang from Viridis ' 
 loin - girdle , and draw out thence flint and steel and tinder , which 
 matter , forsooth , have serve she before in the boat to make fire 
 withal . then she set her hand to her head , and draw forth the tress 
 of hair which Habundia have give she , and which be coil up in the 
 crown of her own abundant lock which deck she so gloriously ; she 
 draw two hair from the say tress , and hold they between her lip 
 while she do up the tress in its place again , and then , pale and 
 trembling , fall to strike a light , and when she have the tinder 
 burning , she cry out : 

 o wood - mother , wood - mother ! how then may we meet again as thou didst 
 promise I , if I die here in this empty waste ? o wood - mother , if 
 thou mightest but come hither for my deliverance ! 

 then she burn the hair one after another , and stand wait , but 
 nought befell a great while , and her heart sicken , and there she 
 stand like a stone . 

 but in awhile , lo ! there come as it be a shadow amidst the mist , or 
 rather lie thereon , faint and colourless , and it be of the shape 
 of the wood - mother , with girt - up gown and bow in hand . birdalone 
 cry aloud with joy , and hasten toward the semblance , but come to 
 it no nigh , and still she go , and the semblance still escape 
 she , and she follow on and on ; and this last long , and fast and 
 fast must she follow lest it vanish , and she gather her skirt 
 into her girdle , and fall to run fleet - foot after the flee 
 shadow , which she love dearly even amidst the jaw of death ; and all 
 her fleetness of foot have Birdalone to put forth in follow up the 
 chase ; but even to die in the pain would she not miss that dear 
 shadow . 

 but suddenly , as she run , the mist be all go from before she , the 
 sun shine hot and cloudless ; there be no shadow or shape of Habundia 
 there , nought but the blue lake and the ugly lip of that hideous 
 desert , with the Sending Boat lie a half score yard from her foot ; 
 and behind she stand up , as it be a wall , the mist from out of 
 which she have come . 

 Forsooth Birdalone be too breathless to cry out her joy , but her 
 heart go nigh to break therewith , and lovely indeed to she be 
 the ripple water and the blue sky ; and she know that her wood - mother 
 have speed a sending to her help , and she fall a - weeping where she 
 stand , for love of her wise mother , and for longing to behold she : 
 she stretch out her arm to the north quarter , and say blessing 
 on she in a voice faint for weariness . then she lay she down on the 
 desert , and rest she with sleep , despite the hot sun , and when she 
 awake , some three hour thereafter , all be as before , save that the 
 sky have now some light - fly cloud , and still be the wall of mist 
 behind she . wherefore she deem she have yet time , and the blue 
 ripple water woo her much - besweate limb ; so she do off her 
 raiment and take the water , and become happy and unweary therein . 
 then she land and stand in the sun to dry she , and so , strengthen 
 with that refreshing , clothe she , and go aboard and do the due 
 rite , and speed over the water , and have soon lose sight of that ugly 
 blotch on the fair face of the Great Water . 


 here end the Second Part of the Water of the Wondrous Isles , which 
 be call of the Wondrous Isles , and begin the Third Part of the 
 say tale , which be call of the Castle of the Quest . 




 the third part : of the CASTLE of the QUEST 




 CHAPTER i. birdalone come to the castle of the QUEST 



 Empty be the day to Birdalone save for her thought , and she sleep 
 not a good while of the night . when she awake in the morning there 
 be no land before she , and she begin to fear somewhat that so it 
 might be many day , and that she might have to fare the water 
 landless , and perchance till she starve for hunger ; for now be 
 there but little victual left of that which the kind Viridis have 
 give she . so she wear the day somewhat uneasily , and by then night 
 fall have eat but little ; yet be that little the last crumb and 
 gobbet of her store . wherefore it be no wonder though she be 
 dismay when she awake early on the morrow , and beheld nought before 
 she save the landless water . 

 but about noon she deem she see a little cloud in the offing that 
 move not as the other cloud , and she watch it closely at first , 
 and it change not any the more , and she grow weary of watch it 
 and strove to sleep , turn her head to the after part of her ferry ; 
 and thus betwixt sleep and wake she wear away three hour : then 
 she stand up and look ahead , and lo , the white cloud have take 
 shape , and be a white castle far away   for the day be exceed 
 clear , sit , as it seem , on the very face of the water . the 
 boat speed on swiftly thitherward , so that it be not right long ere 
 birdalone beheld the green shore on either side of the said castle , 
 and at last , three hour before sunset , she be draw nigh thereto , 
 and behold it all clearly , what it be . 

 it be brand - new , and be fair enough , build part of stone and 
 lime , part of framed work , but be but middling big . as she draw 
 nigh yet , she see that there be folk on the wall of it , and they 
 seem to see she , for a horn be wind from the battlement , and 
 folk be run together to somewhither . and now be Birdalone 
 come so near , that she see the water - gate of the castle , and folk 
 come out thereby on to the landing - place ; and she see presently , 
 that a very tall man with grizzle hair stand foremost of they , and 
 he wave his hand to she , and spake something , but the wind bear the 
 word away from she ; yet she seem to know that this folk would do 
 she to wit that they would have none of she ; and her heart die 
 within she , so faint and hungry as she be . 

 Howsoever the ferry speed on its way swiftly , and in a minute or two 
 have stay itself at the landing - stair , whereabout be gather a 
 score of man , some arm some unarmed , and they seem for the more 
 part to be grey - headed and past middle - age . 

 birdalone stand up in her craft , and the aforesaid tall grey man , who 
 be unarmed , but clothe in knightly raiment , stand on the stair and 
 spake unto she , and say : Lady , this be an house where woman enter 
 never since first the roof be do thereon , which forsooth be but a 
 year ago . we will pray thee therefore to turn thy boat 's head away , 
 and seek some other lodge by the water , either eastward or 
 westward . 

 little know Birdalone of worldly courtesy , or she have make he a 
 sharp answer belike ; but she only look on he ruefully , and say : 
 good warrior , I be come a long way , and may not turn back from mine 
 errand ; and I be now lack victual and hungry , and if ye help I 
 not , it be like that I shall die . much lieth on mine errand , if ye 
 know it . she be weeping - ripe , but refrain her tear , though she 
 lip quiver . she stretch out her hand to the greybeard , and he 
 look on she and find she exceed fair ; and he deem she to be 
 guileless , both because of her simple speech and sweet voice , and the 
 goodliness of her face and eye . but he say : Lady , thine errand 
 hath nought to do with it , it be thy womanhood that bar our door . 
 for all we be bind by oath not to suffer a woman to abide in this 
 castle till our lord take the bann off , and bid we open to woman . 
 she smile faintly , and say : if I might but see thy lord then , 
 since thou art not master here . he say : they be away , and will 
 not be back till to - morrow morning ; and I wot not the hour of their 
 return . and yet , say he , I would we might help thee somewhat . o I 
 pray thee , I pray thee ! she say , or mine errand will come to nought 
 after all . 

 Therewith come another man down the stair , and stand by the old 
 knight and pluck his sleeve , and fall to talk with he softly . 
 this man be by his habit a religious , and be a young man than the 
 other , it might be of five and thirty winter , and he be fair of 
 favour . while they spake together Birdalone sit she down again , and 
 be well - nigh spend . 

 at last the old man spake : Damsel , he say , we deem we may suffer 
 thee to enter the castle since thy need be so great , and have a 
 meal 's meat at our hand , and yet save our oath , if thou depart 
 thence by the landward gate before sunset . will this serve thee ? 
 Fair sir , say Birdalone , it will save my life and mine errand ; I may 
 say no more word for my faintness , else would I thank thee . 

 she stand up on her foot , and the old man - at - arm reach out his 
 hand to she , and she take it and come her way up the stair , but 
 find herself but feeble . but the priest   forsooth he be chaplain 
 of the castle   help she on the other side . but when she stand on 
 the level stone by the water - gate , she turn to the old man and 
 say : one thing I will ask of thee , be this place one of the 
 Wondrous Isles ? the elder shake his head . we know not the Wondrous 
 Isles , say he ; this castle be build on the mainland . her face 
 flush for joy at the word , and she say : one thing I will crave of 
 thee , to wit , that thou wilt leave my barge lie here untouched till 
 thy master come back , and wilt give command that none meddle 
 therewith . 

 he would have answer , but the priest brake in , and say : this will 
 he do , lady , and he be the castellan , and moreover he will swear to 
 obey thee herein . and therewith he draw forth a cross with God 
 nail thereon , and the castellan swear on it with a good will . 

 then the priest draw Birdalone on , and between they they bring she 
 into the great hall , and set she down in a chair and prop she with 
 cushion . and when she be thus at rest , she begin to weep somewhat , 
 and the castellan and the priest stand by and comfort she ; for 
 themseeme , despite her grief , that she have bring the sun into 
 their house . 

 Next be victual bring unto she of broth and venison , and good 
 wine and cate and strawberry ; and she be not so famished but she 
 might eat and drink with a good will . but when she be do , and have 
 rest a little , the castellan stand up and say : Lady , the sun be 
 go off the western window now , and I must save mine oath ; but ere 
 thou depart , I be fain to hear thy voice give I pardon for my 
 evil cheer and the thrusting of thee forth . and therewith he put one 
 knee to the ground , and take her hand and kiss it . but birdalone 
 be grow merry again , and she laugh and say : what pardon thou 
 canst have of I , kind knight , thou hast ; but now methink thou 
 makest overmuch of I , because I be the only woman who hath come into 
 thy castle . I be but a simple maiden , though mine errand be not 
 little . 

 Forsooth she wonder that the stark and gruff old man be so change 
 to she in little space ; for nought she know as yet how the sight of 
 she cast a hot gleed of love into the heart of they who behold she . 

 now Birdalone arise ; but the castellan kneel at her foot , and kiss 
 her hand again , and again , and yet again . then he say : thou art 
 gracious indeed . but methink the father here will lead thee out - a- 
 gate ; for he may show thee a lair , wherein thou shalt be safe enough 
 to - night ; and to - morrow may bring new tiding . 

 so the priest make obeisance to she and lead she down the hall , and 
 the castellan 's eye be follow they till the screen hide they . 
 the priest leave she in the hall - porch a while , and go into the 
 buttery , and come back with a basket of meat and drink , and they go 
 forth at the great gate together , and there be the last of the sun 
 before they . 



 CHAPTER II . of BIRDALONE , and how she rest the night through in a 
 bower without the CASTLE of the quest 



 on a fair smooth road go they amidst of a goodly meadow - land , 
 wherein be little copse here and there . when they be fairly out 
 of the gate , the priest reach for Birdalone 's hand , and she let he 
 take it and lead she along thereby , think no evil ; but he might 
 scarce speak for a while , so great be the stir in his heart at the 
 touch of her bare flesh . but Birdalone spake and say : thou art 
 kind , father , to lead I on my way thus .

 CHAPTER III . how birdalone dight she for meet the CHAMPIONS of 
 the quest

 CHAPTER IV . and now she meet the champion

 CHAPTER V. BIRDALONE have true tokens from the champion of the quest

 skin ; and that make good time for kiss again , as ye may well wot . 
 then she say unto I : and how may I , a poor damsel , give thee 
 gift , and my kindre all greedy about I ? yet would I give thee a 
 gift , such as I may , if I but know what thou wouldst take . now my 
 heart be afire with that kissing of her shoulder , and I say that I 
 would have that very same smock from her body , which then she bore , 
 and that thereof I should deem that I have a rich gift indeed . what ! 
 say she , and wouldst thou have it here and now ? and indeed I think 
 she would have do it off she that minute have I press she , but I 
 lack the boldness thereto ; and I say : Nay , but would she bring it 
 unto I the next time we meet ; and forsooth she bring it fold in a 
 piece of green silk , and dearly have I love it and kiss it 
 sithence . but as for thy smock , I have it fairly wrought and 
 embroider with the flame green branch , as thou seest it , and I 
 give it to she ; but not on the day when she give I the gift ; for the 
 new one be long about do . now this be all the tale , and how 
 Viridis might eke it into a long one , I wot not . but let it be , and 
 tell I , have I win thy smock , or lose it ? 

 birdalone laugh on he and say : well , at least thou shalt have it 
 as a gift ; and thou mayst call it give either by Viridis or I , 
 which thou wilt . but with it go another gift ; which thou mayst 
 have at once since thou must lend I the smock a little long . and 
 therewith she betake he her girdle , and he kiss it , but say : 
 Nay , fair lady , this befitteth well the loveliness of thy body that 
 thou shouldst wear it ; and well it befitteth the truth and love of 
 thy soul toward it for I ; I pray thee to keep it . nevertheless , she 
 say , I will not have it , for it goeth with mine errand that thou 
 take it of I . now I bid thee depart , and send hither thy fellow , 
 the Black Squire . 

 go he then , and anon come the Black Squire , and now that he be 
 alone with Birdalone this first time , he seem moody and downcast , 
 all unlike the two other . he stand a little aloof from Birdalone , 
 and say : what wouldst thou ask of I ? her heart be somewhat 
 chill by his moodiness , for erst have she deem he the kind of 
 the three ; but she say : it be of mine errand to ask of thee 
 concern this foot - gear which Atra lend I until I give it unto 
 thee , if thou be verily her lover . say he : I be verily her lover . 
 birdalone say : then canst thou tell I the manner of thy give 
 these fair shoon unto Atra ? 

 he say : even so ; we be walk together in this country - side and 
 come to a ford of the river , and it be somewhat deep and take I to 
 over the knee , so I bear she over in my arm ; then we go on a 
 little far till we must cross the river back again in another 
 place , and there the ford be shallow , and , the day be hot , Atra 
 must need wade it on her own foot . so she do off hosen and shoon , 
 and I lead she by the hand , and it take she but up to mid - leg . but 
 when we come up out of the water and be on the grass again , I 
 crave the gift of her foot - gear for the love of she , and she give it 
 straightway , and fare home barefoot , for it be over the mead we 
 be wend in early summer , and the grass be thick and soft . but 
 thereafter I do do make the fair shoon which thou hast on thy foot , 
 and give they to she . and , for a far token that my tale be true , 
 I shall tell thee that the name of the first ford we wad that day 
 be the Grey - nag 's Wade , and the second be call Goat Ford . this be 
 all my tale , lady ; be the token true ? 

 true it be , squire , say Birdalone , and be silent awhile , and he 
 also . then she look on he friendly , and say : thou art out of 
 heart as now , my friend . fear not , for thou shalt without doubt see 
 thy speech - friend again . moreover here be a ring which she set upon 
 my finger , bid I give it thee . and she hold it out unto he . 

 he take the ring , and say : yea , it be good that I have it of thee , 
 lest unluck come thereof . she see trouble in his face , but know not 
 what to say to cheer he , and they stand silently face one another 
 for awhile . then he say : let we back to our fellow , and talk it 
 over , what be now to be do . 

 so they go their way to where lay the other two upon the green 
 grass , and the Black Squire lie down beside they ; but Birdalone stand 
 before they and spake unto the three . 



 CHAPTER VI . how the CHAMPIONS would do birdalone to be clothe ANEW in 
 the CASTLE of the QUEST 



 Lords , she say , now be it clear by the token that mine errand be to 
 you and none other ; now therefore be I to tell you what to do to come 
 unto your speech - friend and deliver they and bring they back hither . 
 for this be their case , that they be in captivity in a wonder - isle 
 of this great water , and it be call the Isle of Increase Unsought . 

 spake the Golden Knight : Fair lady , we have hear before that our 
 friend fare hence , or rather be take hence over the water . and 
 that be the cause why we build this castle on the water 's edge , on 
 the very stead where be raise the pavilion , the house make for the 
 lady to abide therein the battle of the Champions . since that 
 time , moreover , many a barge and keel have we thrust out into the 
 water , that we might accomplish the Quest whereunto we be vow ; 
 but ever one way go our seafaring , that when we be come so far 
 out into the water as to lose sight of land , come upon us mist , rise 
 against we dusk and darkness ; and then a fierce driving wind that 
 drave we back to this shore . it be but six day ago since we try 
 this adventure for the last time , and belike the same shall befall we 
 the next time we try it . wherefore I must ask thee , lady , dost thou 
 know any way whereby we may come to the said isle ? for if thou dost , 
 full surely we will try it , whatsoever may be the risk thereby to our 
 body or our soul . 

 full surely I do , say Birdalone ; else how have I come from thence 
 hither mine own self ? and therewith she tell they of the Sending 
 Boat , what it be , and how she have come all the way by mean thereof 
 from the Isle of Increase Unsought ; and they all hearken she 
 heedfully , and wonder both at the sorcery , and the valiant heart of 
 she who have drive it as she would in despite of the evil . but in 
 the end she spake and say : lord , ye have now hear some deal of my 
 story , even that which concern you thereof ; and which must need be 
 tell at once : wherefore doubtless ye shall fare unto your speech- 
 friend by this ferry in the very wise that I shall show you ; unless 
 perchance ye deem that I have be lie and make light tale to 
 you , as , sooth to say , I deem ye think it not . 

 spake the Golden Knight : Damsel , in all wise we trow in thee and thy 
 tale . and God forbid that we should tarry ! go we hence this very 
 day . 

 Yea , but hearken , say the Black Squire : be it not a part of this 
 damsel 's errand that she should deliver to we the raiment of our 
 friend , which now she beareth on her own body , that we may bear it 
 back unto they ? 

 Sooth be that , say Birdalone , and ye may well wot that this may be 
 nought but needful , whereas the say lady be all beset by 
 sorcery . 

 see ye then , fellow , say the Black Squire , it may not be to - day nor 
 yet to - morrow that we may take the road . for ye wot that there be no 
 woman 's gear in all the castle , and we must need send otherwhere to 
 seek it . 

 look thou , maiden , say the Golden Knight , laughing , how duly this 
 young knight thinketh of thee ; whereas I , who be his elder , and 
 should be wise than he , be but heedless of thee . I pray thy pardon . 

 moreover , say the Black Squire , there may well be wisdom in abide ; 
 for it be to be think that our dear love consider this , and know 
 what the time of tarrying should be , and have so dight their matter 
 as to fit in therewith ; and I may not deem it of they that they would 
 have we array this our dear sister and theirs in unseemly wise . Nay , 
 for that would be an ill beginning of this deal of the Quest . 

 now all yeasaid this gladly ; and the Green Knight say : it be not 
 so ill do that we should see more of our sister here ere we depart , 
 and hear more of her tale ; for meseemeth she begin it erewhile but 
 half - way . and he turn to Birdalone , and take her hand and caress 
 it . 

 birdalone smile on they somewhat shyly , and thank they ; but bade 
 they spend as little time as might be on her arrayal . for , say she , 
 though those lady may well have reckon on the time of the arrayal 
 of my body , yet surely also they shall have reckon with the eager 
 fire of love in the heart of you , and the haste it shall breed 
 therein . 

 well pleased be they with that word of her , but none the less send 
 two sergeant and a squire with lead horse unto the cheaping - town , a 
 goodly and great town hight Greenford , which be some twenty mile 
 thence , with the errand to bring back with they a good shaper and 
 embroideress , and sewing - woman , and cloth and silk and linen , and all 
 thing needful . 

 as for jewel , each one of they be fain to give she something which 
 he prize , and fair and rich be the gift , though they have not be 
 make for woman . as a fair SS collar of gold , which the Golden Knight 
 give she , and a girdle of broad golden plate , work beauteously , 
 which be the gift of the Black Squire . albeit he do not offer to 
 clasp it round her loin , as she deem he would ; for when the Green 
 Knight bring his gift , a great gold ring , very ancient of fashion , 
 he would have her turn back the sleeve from her fore - arm , that he 
 might set his dwarf - wrought gold upon the bare flesh ; neither do he 
 refrain he from kiss it withal . 

 but the messenger come back with their work - woman and stuff early 
 on the morrow ; and now be change all the manner of the womanless 
 castle , and man be full merry therein . 



 CHAPTER VII . of BIRDALONE , how she tell the champion all her TALE 



 it be a matter of eight day , the making of all Birdalone 's raiment , 
 and meanwhile she be ever with the three Champions , either all three 
 together , or one or other of they . and as to their manner with she , 
 ever be the Golden Knight of somewhat sober demeanour , as if he be 
 an old man than he verily be . the Green Knight be for ever 
 praise Birdalone 's beauty to her face , and seem to find it no 
 easy matter to keep his eye off she , and somewhat he weary she 
 with kiss and caress ; but a gay and sportive lad he be ; and when 
 she rebuke he for his overmuch fondness , as now and again she do , 
 he would laugh at himself along with she ; and in sooth she deem he 
 heart - whole , and of all truth to Viridis , and oft he would talk of 
 she to Birdalone , and praise her darling beauty to she , and tell of 
 his longing for his love aloof . only , quoth he , here art thou , my 
 sister , dwell amongst we , and shed thy fragrance on we , and 
 show to we , wilt thou , wilt thou not , as do the flower , all the 
 grace and loveliness of thee ; and thou so tender of heart withal ,

 my sister , and that my love be , woe 's I ! far away . so thou wilt 
 pardon I , wilt thou not ? yea , verily , say she , with a whole heart . 
 yet thou need not reach out for my hand ; thou hast have enough of 
 it this morning . and she hide it , laugh , in the fold of her gown ;

 together again . saw thou ever so fair a damsel ? never , she say , 
 and surely there be none fair in all the world . so hold thee aloof 
 now for a while , and think of she . 

 as for the Black Squire , hight Arthur , Birdalone be trouble for 
 he , and he make she somewhat sad . true it be that he come not 
 before she again so moody and downcast as when he be give she the 
 token ; yet she deem that he enforce himself to seem of good cheer . 
 furthermore , though he seek her company ever , and that lonely with 
 he , and would talk with she almost as one man with another , though 
 with a certain tenderness in his voice , and look earnestly on she 
 the while , yet never would he take her hand , or touch she in any 
 wise . and true it be that she long for the touch of his hand . 

 on the third day of her sojourn in the Castle of the Quest , Birdalone 
 take heart at the much egging of her friend , as they sit all 
 together in the meadow without the castle , to tell they all the story 
 of she ; she hide none , save concern the wood - mother , for she deem 
 that her sweet friend would love she the well if she babble not of 
 she . 

 so the Champions hearken her tell the tale in her clear lovely 
 voice , and great be their love and pity for the poor lonely maiden . 
 and in especial clear it be to see that they be sore move when 
 she tell how she first come on the Sending Boat , and how the witch- 
 wife torment her innocent body for that guilt . then Baudoin lay 
 his hand upon her head , and spake : poor child , much indeed hast thou 
 suffer ! and now I will say it , that it be for we and our love 
 that thou hast bear all this anguish of captivity and toil and 
 stripe . 

 but Hugh lean over to she , as she sit with her head hang down , 
 and kiss she cheek , and say : yea ! and I be not there to smite

 anguish , as I take my light pleasure about these free meadow . and 
 he turn very red , and go nigh to weep . 

 Arthur sit still with his eye bent down on the ground , and he say 
 nothing ; and birdalone glance on he wistfully ere she go on with 
 her tale . and she go on and tell closely all that have happen 
 unto she in the crossing of the water and on the Isle of Increase 
 Unsought , and the other Wonder Isles ; and she deem it not too much 
 that she should tell it twice over , nor they that twice over they 
 should hearken it . 

 that same evening as Birdalone walk by herself in the castle 
 pleasance , she see Arthur peer about as if he be seek 
 someone ; so she stand forth , and ask he be he seek aught ; and 
 he say : Thee be I seek . but she durst not ask he what he 
 would , but stand silent and tremble before he , till he take she 
 hand , and spake not loud but eagerly . 

 after what thou hast tell we to - day , I seem to know thee what thou 
 art ; and I tell thee that it be a pain and grief to I to leave thee , 
 yea to leave thee be it but for a minute . o I pray thee pity I 
 for the sundering . and therewith he turn about and hasten into 
 the castle . but Birdalone stand there with her heart beat fast

 she . but she say to herself that it be no wonder though she feel 
 so happy , see that she have find out that , despite her fear , this 
 one of her friend love she no less well than the other . and then 
 she spake it in a soft voice that she would indeed pity he for the 
 sundering , yea , and herself also . 

 nevertheless , when they meet thereafter , his demeanour to she be none 
 otherwise than it have be ; but she no long heed this since now 
 she trowe in he . 



 CHAPTER VIII . in the MEANWHILE of the departing of the CHAMPIONS , 
 they would pleasure birdalone with FEATS of ARMS and GAMES of PROWESS 



 pass the day now speedily , and the three Champions do what they

 show she of arm , and they tilt together courteously ; and the

 then the young man run afoot before she for the prize of a belt and

 and in all these pastime , whatso they be , Birdalone bear herself

 with Sir Aymeris , the grizzle - haired castellan , she foregather also

 day . 



 CHAPTER IX . BIRDALONE COMETH before the CHAMPIONS in her new ARRAY 



 now the time be come when Birdalone have all her gear ready , and the 
 woman be to abide in the castle as her serve - damsel while the 
 Champions be away . 

 so now in the summer eve , an hour before sunset , Birdalone do on the 
 rich of her new raiment , and come into the hall where sit the

 have on a green gown with broidered sleeve , and thereover a white

 rather sunrise than sunset it seem , as verily birdalone she come

 countenance smile with love . the man stand up all , and would come

 each in his place till she stand before they . 

 up the hall then she walk , and every step of hers seem lovely

 last deal of your Quest ; and it be I that have bring you to this ,

 wherefore I pray you to love I ever , and bear I ever in your mind .

 I find thee . brother , will ye not swear the same ? and this be but 
 thy due , maiden , for I declare unto thee , that when thou didst enter

 unto we . 

 Thereon the other two take the Rood and swear upon it : and Hugh be 
 hush and meek and sad - faced after he have swear ; but Arthur the 
 Black Squire bow down his head and weep , and his fellow marvel 
 nought thereat , neither do Birdalone ; and all her body yearn 
 toward he to solace he . 

 now turn Sir Baudoin to the castellan and say : Sir Aymeris , I 
 will now swear thee to guard this lady as the apple of thine eye 
 while we three be away , and therein to spare neither thyself nor 
 other . for thou se well what grief it would be to we if she come 
 to any harm . 

 and to I also , say the castellan . and therewith he swear upon the 
 Rood , and then come round the table , and knelt before Birdalone , and 
 kiss her hand . 

 thereafter be they all silent a space ; and then come Birdalone to

 beyond the castle , and never but within a half bowshot , save thou be 
 well accompany . for there be man of violence dwell no great way 
 off , reiver and rover , who would be well pleased to take from we 
 anything which we deem dear ; besides other who would think the 
 lifting of such a jewel good hap indeed . Sir Aymeris , have a care of 
 the Red Knight ; and if thou mightest come by a few more stout lad , 
 to wage they , it be well . 

 birdalone heed not what the castellan answer , such a shaft of joy 
 go to her heart when she hear that friend speak her own name in 
 such wise as he have never do erst , and that before they all . she 
 but murmur some yeasay to that which Arthur have speak unto she ,

 so there they sit and talk a while in dear and pleasant converse ; 
 and Hugh fall to ask she of her life in the House under the Wood , 
 and she answer all frankly and simply , and the more she tell the 
 dearer she seem to they . 

 thus draw night in , till folk come flockmeal into the hall ; for need 
 must be feast and banquet for triumph of the furtherance of the 
 Quest ; and the most of man be merry ; but somewhat sober be all 
 the three Champions , so that whoso run might read it in their face . 
 as for Birdalone , she show cheerful to all that folk which love 
 she and praise she ; but inwardly sorrow have come home to her heart . 



 CHAPTER X. the champion go their way in the SENDING BOAT 



 when the sun be arise on the morrow the three Champions go down 
 to the landing - place , and there be none with they ; for they have 
 give command that no man should pry into their doing . Thither to 
 they cometh Birdalone , clothe no more in her gay attire , but in a 
 strait black coat and with unshod foot ; and she look no sorry 
 than she be . 

 by Birdalone 's rede the Champions bear down in their own hand the 
 victual and weapon and armour that they need for the voyage ; for 
 she know not but that the Sending Boat might take it amiss that any 
 should touch she save the sender . and when they have do lading 
 she , then all four stand together by the water 's edge , and birdalone 
 spake to her friend , and again bid they beware of the wile of the 
 Isle of Nothing ; and again she tell they of the woful image of the 
 Isle of king and the Isle of Queens , and the strange folk of the 
 Isle of the Young and the Old . then she say : now when ye come to 
 the Isle of Increase Unsought , what think ye to do ? say the Green 
 Knight : if I might rule , we should go straight up to the witch 
 sit in her hall , as thou told we , my dear , and then and there 
 smite the head from off she . his eye flash and his brow knit , 
 and so fierce he look that birdalone shrink back from he ; but the 
 Black Squire smile and say : it may come to the smiting off of 
 head in the end ; yet must we so fashion our carving , that it avail 
 we for the freeing of our friend ; else may the witch die , and the 
 secret of the prison - house die with she . how sayest thou , dear 
 Birdalone ? 

 she redden at the caress of his voice , and answer : by my rede ye 
 shall seek and find your speech - friend ere ye make open war upon the 
 witch ; else may her malice destroy they ere ye undo she . her face 
 flush yet more as she spake again : but concern all thing , I 
 deem that Atra may give you the good rede , when ye have meet the 
 love ; for that she knoweth more of the isle and its guile than the 
 other . 

 Quoth Baudoin : Herein be wisdom , sweet maiden , for as guileless as 
 thou mayst be ; and so far as we may we shall follow thy rede ; but all 
 lieth in the fathom of the come time . and now this moment be the 
 moment of sundering and farewell . 

 come he then to Birdalone and take his two hand about her head , and 
 lift her face unto he , and kiss it kindly , as a father might 
 kiss a daughter , and say : farewell , dear child , and take heed to 
 the word that Arthur spake yesterday , and go not from the castle even 
 a little way save with good and sure company . 

 then come Hugh to she , and take her hand somewhat timidly ; but she 
 put up her face to he in simple wise , and he kiss either cheek of 
 she , and say no more than : Farewell , Birdalone ! 

 lastly come Arthur , and stand before she a little ; and then he kneel 
 down on the stone before she and kiss her foot many time , and she 
 shudder and catch her breath as they feel his kiss ; but neither 
 he nor she spake a word , and he stand up and turn away at once 
 toward the Sending Boat , and board she first of the three ; and the 
 other follow straightway . 

 thereafter the Champions bar each an arm , and let blood flow thence 
 into a bowl , and reddened stem and stern of their barge , and then all 
 three spake the spell together thus , as Birdalone have teach they : 


 the red raven - wine now 
 Hast thou drunk , stern and bow : 
 wake then , and awake , 
 and the northern way take ! 
 the way of the Wenders forth over the flood , 
 for the will of the Senders be blent with the blood . 


 go all as before thereafter , that the Sending Boat stir under 
 they , and then turn about and point she bow to the northward , 
 and speed swiftly over the water . it be a fair sunny day , with no 
 cloud , nought save the summer haze lie on the lake far away . 
 birdalone stand watch the speeding of the boat , till she could see 
 it no long , not even as a fleck on the face of the water . then 
 she turn away and go toward her chamber , say to herself that 
 the sundering be easy to bear than she have deem it would be , and 
 that she have a many thing to do that day . but when she come into 
 her chamber , and shut the door , she look about she on the thing 
 which have grow so familiar to she in these few latter day , and she 
 stand watch the bright sunshine that stream across the floor and 
 lie warm upon her foot ; then she take three step toward the window , 
 and see the lake lie all a - glitter under the sun , and her heart 
 fail her withal , and she have no might so much as to think about her 
 sorrow and caress it , but fall down where she be swoon on to the 
 floor , and lie there , while all the house begin to stir about she . 


 here end the Third Part of the Water of the Wondrous Isles , which be 
 call of the Castle of the Quest , and begin the fourth Part of the 
 say tale , which be call of the day of Abiding . 




 the fourth PART : of the day of abiding 




 CHAPTER I. of BIRDALONE 's GRIEF ; and of LEONARD the CHAPLAIN 



 now come Birdalone to herself , and that be but little joy unto she , 
 and she yet lie still on the floor for a while , for she loathe the 
 hour that be to come . then the life stir in she , and whereas she 
 would not that her woman should find she there , she stand up , and 
 clothe herself somewhat more seemly ; yet she do on her black raiment ; 
 and determine in her mind that nought would she wear save black 
 unadorned while her friend be away . 

 she betake she now to the chamber where her woman be gather 
 together , and watch they work a while , but spake nought . then 
 she go her way into the pleasance , and pace the plashed alley up 
 and down , let the tear run down from she as they would . then 
 she turn back into the castle , and go out - a - gate and walk over 
 the meadow a little , and might well have go far than wisdom 
 would . but the castellan espy she from a window , and come hurry 
 out after she , and with many prayer for pardon , bring she back 
 again , babble to she by the way ; but not a word might he get from 
 she ; and when he come into the hall with she , and , after his will not , 
 knelt down to kiss her hand , she catch they away from he 
 peevishly , and be sorry for it thereafter . 

 long she sit in the hall , scarce move , till she hear one enter 
 from the screen , and lo it be Leonard the chaplain . he come she 
 way , and show her rueful countenance ; and pity of he smite she , 
 and she remember therewith how they first go out of gate 
 together ; and at the thought thereof her tear brake forth again , but 
 she make he a sign with her hand to sit down beside she , and he do 
 so ; and when she might for her weeping , she look kindly on he , and 
 he fall to talk , make as if he note not her tear and sorrow ; but 
 she answer he little , for she have shame to begin the talk 
 concern the Champions and their Quest , and their departure ; yet 
 might she not bring her tongue to make any speech else . but 
 presently he take up the word , and ask she how long a while she 
 deem they would be away , and she answer , smile on he for 
 thank , and have reckon the day on her finger : if all go 
 well than well , they may be back in ten day ' time . say the 
 chaplain : there be long while of wait in most man 's life . 
 Yea , she say , but this be the delay at the good ; it may be far 
 long ; for how may we tell what hap may be ? 

 Yea , say Leonard , shall we then call it twenty day , or thirty ? 
 Forsooth , that may be long for thee ; though there be some who must 
 need endure hope defer a deal long . but it may run out long 
 than even thirty day , thy waiting - tide . 

 she answer not , and he say : Whenso the time hang heavy on hand 
 with thee , if thou hast will to fare abroad out of the castle , I 
 shall be ever at hand to guide thee . indeed , I wot that the 
 castellan will be loth to let thee go ; but he be old and straitlace : 
 and yet withal he wotteth , as do we all , that there be now little 
 peril or none be we to fare a five mile or more , whereas we be as 
 good as at peace for the last five day with all save the Red Knight , 
 and of he we wot that he be go into another land with as many of 
 his folk as be not need for the warding of his hold . 

 I thank thee , say Birdalone , but it be like to be my will not to 
 fare out - a - gate till the Champions come back home . I be glad e'en 
 now when the castellan fetch I in again : to say sooth , fear of 
 peril have just enter my heart when he come up with I . 

 the priest seem somewhat chapfallen at her answer . he spake little 
 more , and presently he stand up , make his obeisance , and depart . 



 CHAPTER II . birdalone LEARNETH LORE of the PRIEST . ten day of 
 waiting wear 



 wear that day and the next , and Birdalone fall to talk with her 
 woman , whereof be five now leave ; and four of they be young , the 
 eld scarce of thirty summer , and the fifth be a woman of sixty , 
 both wise and kind . all these tell she somewhat of their own life 
 when she ask they ; and some withal tell of folk whom they have know 
 or hear tell of . and well pleased be birdalone to hear thereof , 
 and learn more of the way of the world , and quick - witted she be at 
 the lesson , so that she need not to ask many question . 

 furthermore , she take to she broider again , and fall to do a 
 goodly pair of shoon for Atra , since she have wear those borrow one 
 somewhat hardly . and the woman wonder at her needlework , so 
 marvellous fine as it be , and how that in little space of time be 
 come flower and tree , and bird and beast , all lovely ; and they 
 say that the faery must have learn she that craft . but she 
 laugh and redden , and thought of the wood - mother ; and , sit 
 there within the four wall , she long for the oak - glade , and the

 now it be the ninth day since the Champions be go , and all that

 some three hour after she wake up , and hear a sound of folk

 face be all wet with the tear . 

 the sun be high now , and his beam be cast back from the ripple of 
 the lake , and shine waver on the wall of the chamber , the window 
 whereof give on to the water . then come a hand on the latch of the

 toward , Catherine ? the maid say : yes , my lady ; for early after

 hath be hurt in some fray , and keepeth his bed ; wherefore the land

 Catherine ; I shall lie a little long ; depart now . 

 the woman go her way ; and when she be go , Birdalone weep and

 morrow morning . and she stay her weeping , and be calm . but

 but at last she clothe herself in haste , and go stealthily from the

 tower - top that be nighest , and look through the door on to the 
 lead , and see no one there ; so she go out , and stand by the 
 battlement , and gaze long over the water , but see neither boat nor 
 burn mountain come towards she . 



 CHAPTER III . now would birdalone RIDE abroad 



 after a while she come down again , and go to the woman , and sit 
 work with they a while , and so wear away two hour . then she send 
 for the priest and have her lesson of he ; and when she have be at it

 nought loth he be thereto ; forsooth he have be long to pray she

 strive to shape the letter ; nay , while must he touch her hand 
 with his , and hold it . wherefore now he promise himself a taste of 
 Paradise . withal he be full meet to learn she , whereas he be one 
 of the good of scribe , and a fair - writer full handy . 

 so they fall to the lesson , and she become eager thereover , and 
 learn fast , and clave to the work , while his soul be torment

 the longing for her speech - friend , and she give the priest leave for 
 that day , but suffer he to kiss her hand for wage . 

 then she hurry up to the tower - top , when the afternoon be wear 
 into evening ; and abode there a long while look over the water ,

 woman . 

 the next day be like unto this ; nought betid , and she wear the hour

 on the third of these day she call the castellan to she for a

 go , and many hap betide in such tale . now I beseech thee torment

 his word solace she much for that time , whereas she see that he

 deal of that be I wax white and faint . and thou wouldst not have 
 I fall sick on thine hand now , wouldst thou ? 

 Nay , surely , lady , say Sir Aymeris ; this very day I will ride out

 for fear of mishap . say Birdalone , knit her brow : Nay , 
 knight , I need not thy man - at - arm ; I would fain go free and alone . 
 for hast thou not hear how that the Red Knight be hurt and keepeth

 stealing of it if he may . 

 Laughed Birdalone , and say : but how if the say jewel hath a will , 
 and leg and foot thereto , and be ready to take the peril on she , and

 then , say the castellan , I shall fetch thee back , and , though it be

 again laugh Birdalone , and say : Hearken , whereto cometh all this 
 kneeling and hand - kissing ! but bear in mind , fair lord , how once on

 change , and mayhappen they may change yet again . but tell I , be I

 CHAPTER IV . of birdalone 's faring ABROAD 



 indeed Birdalone long on any term to be out - a - gate and to have 
 some joy of the summer ; for now she begin to see that she might have 
 to abide some while ere her friend should come to she in the Castle 
 of the Quest ; and she be angry with herself that her longing be 
 thus waste she , and she rebuke herself and say : where be now 
 that birdalone who let but few day go by without some joyance of the 
 earth and its creature ? she who bear lightly the toil of a thrall , 
 and gibe and mocking and stripe ? surely this be grievous folly , 
 that I should be worsen since I have come to be the friend of 
 gentle lady , and noble champion , and mighty warrior . have it not 
 be well to have abide under the witch - wife 's hand ? for not 
 every day nor most day do she torment I . but now for many day 
 there have be pain and grief and heart - sickness hour by hour ; and 
 every hour have I dread the coming of the next hour , till I know 
 not how to bear it . 

 so she strove with herself , and become of well heart , and set 
 herself strongly to the learning of the clerkly lore ; she gather 
 her wit together , and no long look for every day and every hour 
 to bring about the return of the Champions , nor blame the day and 
 the hour because they fail therein , and in all wise she strove to 
 get through the day unworn by vain longing . 

 wherefore , on a day when three whole week be go since the day of 
 departure , she be glad when the castellan come to she and say : 
 Lady , these two day I have have man out to spy the land , and their 
 word go that nought be stir which a score of we well - arm 
 might have cause to fear ; wherefore to - morrow , if it be thy will , we 
 shall bring thee out - a - gate , and so please thee , shall be in no 
 haste to come back , but may lie out in the wildwood one night , and 
 come back at our leisure on the morrow of to - morrow . how sayest thou 
 of thy pleasure herein ? 

 she thank he , and yeasaid it eagerly , and next morning they set 
 forth ; and Birdalone have with her three of the woman , and they have 
 sumpter - beast with they , and tent for Birdalone and her maid . 

 so they ride by pleasant way and fair meadow , and the weather be 
 good , for it be now the first day of July , and all be as lovely as 
 might be ; and for that while Birdalone cast off all her care , and 
 be merry , and of many word and sweet ; and all the folk rejoice 
 thereat , for all love she in the Castle of the Quest , besides those 
 one or two that love her overmuch . 

 ride they thus a twelve mile or more , and then they come , as their 
 purpose be , to the beginning of a woodland plenteous of venison , and 
 they hunt here , and Birdalone take her part therein , and all 
 praise her woodcraft ; albeit because of she go a head or two free 
 that have fall else , whereas of the carle hunter be some who 
 deem the body of her well worth look on than the quarry . 

 Howsoever , they slay of hind and roe and other wood - cattle what they 
 would , some deal for their supper in the wilderness , some to bear 
 home to the castle . but when night be nigh at hand they make stay 
 in a fair wood - lawn about which run a clear stream , whereby they 
 pitch the lady ' tent ; and Birdalone and hers go down into the 
 water and wash the weariness off they ; and her lady wonder at 
 the deftness of Birdalone 's swimming ; for they bath in a pool 
 somewhat great into which the stream widen , so that there be space 
 enough for her therein . 

 by then they be washen and clothe goodly in raiment which they have 
 bring on the sumpter , the man have light fire and be cook 
 the venison , and anon there be supper and banquet in the wildwood , 
 with drinking of wine and pleasant talk and the telling of tale and 
 singing of minstrelsy ; and so at last , when night be well worn , and 
 out in the open meadow the eastern sky be wax grey , then 
 Birdalone and her lady go to bed in their fair tent , and the 
 man - at - arm lie down on the greensward under the bare heaven . 



 CHAPTER V. SIR AYMERIS SHOWETH birdalone the MOUNTAINS afar off 



 when it be morning and they arise , the day be as fair as yesterday , 
 and folk be even as joyous as they have be then , all but 
 Birdalone , and she be silent and downcast , even when she come forth 
 from the fresh water into the sweetness of the midsummer wood . she 
 have dream in the night that she be all alone in the Castle of the 
 Quest , and that her old mistress come to she from out of the Sending 
 Boat to fetch she away , and bring she aboard , and strip she of 
 her rich garment and sit face she , draw ugsome grimace at she ; 
 and she think she know that her friend be all dead and go , and 
 she have none to pity or defend she . then somehow be they two , the 
 witch and she , amidmost of the Isle of Nothing , and the witch draw 
 close anigh she , and be just go to whisper into her ear something 
 of measureless horror , when she awake ; and the sun be bright outside 
 the shaded whiteness of her tent ; the shadow of the leaf be 
 dance on the ground of it ; the morning wind be rustle the tree- 
 bough , and the ripple of the stream be tinkle hard by . at first

 of the other . 

 that see Sir Aymeris the castellan ; and when they have break fast and

 now they ride fair and softly by thicket and copse and glade of the

 beyond they . 

 when Birdalone 's eye beheld this new thing , of a sudden all care

 cry out : oh ! but thou art beautiful , o earth , thou art beautiful ! 
 then she sit gaze on it , while the greyhead turn and smile on 
 she , well pleased of her pleasure .

 he , yet I doubt if thou wilt like it the well , the nigher thou art . 
 ah ! she say , but if I be only amidst it , and a part of it , as once 
 I be of the woodland ! 

 so thitherward they ride over the unharvested mead , and see hart and 
 hind thereon , and wild kine , and of small deer great plenty , but of 
 tame beast none ; and the hill be before they like a wall . but as 
 they draw nigh , they see where the say wall of the hill be 
 cleave by a valley narrow and steep - sided , that go right athwart 
 the lie of the hill ; the say valley be but little grassed , and the 
 bare rock be crow - black . when they have go a little far , 
 they could see that the ground near the foot of the hill rise in 
 little knoll and ridge , but these be low and few about the 
 entry into that valley . also presently they come upon a stream which 
 run out of the say valley , and Sir Aymeris say that this be the 
 water whereby they have lie last night ; albeit here it be little 
 indeed . 

 now when they have ride some five mile over the plain , they come 
 amongst those knoll at the mouth of the valley , and Sir Aymeris lead 
 birdalone up to the top of one of the high of they , and thence 
 they could look into that dale and see how it wind away up toward 
 the mountain , like to a dismal street ; for not only be it but 
 little grassed , but withal there be neither tree nor bush therein . 
 moreover , scatter all about the bottom of the dale be great 
 stone , which look as if they have once be set in some kind of 
 order ; and that the more whereas they be not black like the rock 
 of the dale - side , but pale grey of hue , so that they look even as 
 huge sheep of the giant feed down the dale . 

 then spake birdalone : verily , sir knight , thou saidst but sooth that 
 I should see thing new and strange . but shall we go a little way 
 into this valley to - day ? Nay , lady , say Sir Aymeris , nor to - morrow , 
 nor any day uncompelle ; neither shall we go nigh unto it than now 
 we be . wherefore not ? say Birdalone , for meseemeth it be as the 
 gate of the mountain ; and fain be I in the mountain . 

 Lady , say the castellan , overmuch perilous it be to ride the 
 valley , which , as thou sayest , be the very gate of the mountain . 
 for the say dale , which hight the Black Valley of the Greywethers , 
 hath a bad name for the haunting of unmanlike wight , against which 
 even our man - at - arm might make no defence . and if any might escape 
 they , and win through the gate and up into the mountain , I wot not 
 if suchlike devil and thing unkent be there in the mountain - land , 
 but of a sooth there be fierce and wild man , like enough to devil , 
 who know no peace , and slay whatsoever cometh unto they , but if they 
 themselves be slay of they . 

 well , say Birdalone , then to - day , at least , we go not into the dale ; 
 but know thou any tale of these wild place ? many have I hear , 
 say he , but I be an ill minstrel and should spoil they in the 
 telling . ask they of Sir Leonard our priest , he knoweth of they 
 well than other , and hath a tongue duly shapen for tell they . 

 birdalone answer nought thereto ; she but turn her horse 's head 
 and ride down the knoll ; and so they come unto their company , and all 
 go their way toward the Castle of the Quest . 

 Nought befell they on their way home ; but the nigh they come to the 
 castle the more pensive wax Birdalone , and , though she hide it , when

 she think to have one rush out and cry : tiding , tiding ! 
 they be come . 

 Nowise it so befell ; they be no more come than be the Day of Doom . 
 and a little after they be within gate ; it be night , and 
 birdalone creep wearily up to her chamber , and gat to bed , and so

 CHAPTER VI . birdalone HEARETH tell TALES of the black VALLEY of the 
 greywether 



 on the morrow be Birdalone heavy of heart than ever yet , and 
 weary for tiding ; and she wonder how she could have be so 
 joyous that day in the wildwood . yet she think much of the Valley 
 of the greywether , and that solace she somewhat after a while , so 
 sore she long to go thither ; and , as ' tis say , one nail knock out 
 the other . so that morning , when she have have her lesson of priest 
 Leonard , she spake thereof to he , and tell he what Sir Aymeris have 
 say concern his knowledge thereof ; and she ask he what he 
 know . 

 I have be there , say he . she start at that word and say : do 
 aught of evil befall thee ? 

 Nay , say he , but a great fear and dread hang about I ; and ' tis say 
 that they try their luck overmuch who go thither twice . 

 birdalone say : tell I now of the tale that be tell of that 
 valley . Quoth Leonard : they be many ; but the main of they be this : 
 that those greywether be giant of yore agone , or landwight , 
 carle , and quean , who have be turn into stone by I wot not what 
 deed ; but that while they come alive again , and can walk and talk as 
 erst they do ; and that if any man may be so bold as to abide the 
 time of their awakening , and in the first moment of their change may 
 frame word that crave the fulfilment of his desire , and if therewith 
 he be both wise and constant , then shall he have his desire fulfil 
 of these wight , and bear his life back again from out the dale . and 
 thus must he speak and no otherwise : o Earth , thou and thy first 
 child , I crave of you such and such a thing , whatsoever it may be . 
 and if he speak more than this , then be he undo . he shall answer 
 no question of they ; and if they threaten he he shall not pray they 
 mercy , nor quail before their uplifted weapon ; nor , to be short , 
 shall he heed they more than if they still be stone unchanged . 
 moreover , when he hath say his say , then shall these wight throng 
 about he and offer he gold and gem , and all the wealth of the 
 earth ; and if that be not enough , they shall bring he the goodly 
 of woman , with nought lack in her shape , but lack all raiment , 
 so that he shall see she as she be verily shapen . but whoso shall 
 take any one of all these gift be lose for ever , and shall become 
 one of that Stony People ; and whoso naysayeth they all until the cock 
 crow , and abideth steady by his one craving , shall win fulfilment 
 thereof , and , as some say , all those gift aforesaid ; for that the 
 Stony People may not abide the day to take they back again . 

 he be silent therewith , and nought spake Birdalone , but look down 
 on the ground , and longing encompass her soul . then the priest 
 spake again : this be a fair adventure , lady , for a hapless one , 
 but for the happy it be a fool 's errand . she answer not , and 
 they part for that time . 

 but the next week , there be yet no tiding come to hand , Birdalone 
 pray the castellan to take she out - a - gate again , that she might 
 once more behold the mountain , and the gate thereof ; and he yeasaid 
 her asking , and go with she , well accompany , as before ; but this 
 time , by Birdalone 's will , they ride straight to the plain aforesaid , 
 and again she look into that dale of the Greywethers from the 
 knoll . somewhat belated they be , so that they might not get back 
 to the castle before dusk , wherefore again they lie out in the 
 wildwood , but there lack somewhat of the triumph and joyance which 
 they have have that other day . they come back to the castle on the 
 morrow somewhat after noon , and find no news there ; nor , to say 
 sooth , do Birdalone look for any ; and her heart be heavy . 



 CHAPTER VII . birdalone beguileth the priest to help she to outgoing 



 now have the time so wear that the season be in the first day of 
 August , and weariness and heartsickness increase on Birdalone again , 
 and she begin to look pined and pale . yet when she spake of the 
 tarrying of the Champions both to the castellan and Sir Leonard the

 whatlike the adventure be ; and neither of those two seem in

 Thrice in these last day do Birdalone go out - a - gate with Sir 
 Aymeris and his company ; and the last of the three time the journey

 Birdalone 's pleasure of the sight of it afar off mar by her

 and come home safely to the castle . 

 on the morrow she sit with Sir Leonard the priest over the writing 
 lesson , and she let it be long , and oft he touch her hand , so that 
 the sweetness of unfulfilled desire go deep to his heart . 

 at last birdalone look up and say : friend , I would ask thee if 
 thou se any peril in my enter the Black Valley of the 
 greywether by daylight if I leave it by daylight ? alone ? quoth he . 
 Yea , she say , alone . he ponder a little , and then say : sooth to 
 say I deem the peril little in the valley itself , if thou be not 
 overcome by terror there . yea , for my part I be not all so sure that 
 thou shalt see the wonder of the Stony Folk come alive ; for ' tis 
 not say that they quicken save on certain night , and chiefly on 
 Midsummer Night ; unless it be that the trier of the adventure be some 
 one fat above other thereto ; as forsooth thou mayst be . and as
