 the SEVENTH PART : the day of return 




 CHAPTER I. SIR HUGH ASKETH birdalone where she would have the ABODE 
 of their fellowship to be 



 on the next day , they arise and be glad , and it be to they as if 
 the sun of the early summer have arise for nought save to shine on 
 their happy day . and they go about from place to place whereas 
 tiding have befall Birdalone ; and she serve they one and all as if 
 she be their handmaid , and they love she and caress she , and have 
 be fain to do all her will do they but know it . 

 in this wise wear day after day till June begin to wane , and then on 
 a time come Hugh unto Birdalone , and spake unto she and say : all we 
 have be talk together , and I be send to ask thee what be in thy 
 mind as to abide here or go elsewhither . for now that we be 
 come together again , not for all the kingdom of the world would we 
 sunder again ; and above all , none of we would leave thee , o my 
 sister . but if thou wilt come with I to our land under the Green 
 Mountains , there be for thee a pleasant place and a fair dwelling , 
 and honour from all folk , and our love that shall never leave thee ; 
 and I , and Arthur my brother , we shall win fame together amongst the 
 knighthood , and thou shalt be proud and glad both of he and of I . 

 she say : and if I may not go with thee thither , what other way be 
 there to escape the sundering ? say hugh : this , that thou choose in 
 the world what land liketh thee for a dwelling - place , and we will go 
 with thee and leave thee never , and thou shalt be our lady and queen . 
 then he laugh and say : yet , our lady , I have leave behind I under 
 the Green Mountains certain thing which I love , as two fair women- 
 child , and a squire or two whose father serve my father , and 
 whose child I would should serve my child . and moreover I have 
 leave there certain matter of avail , my wealth and livelihood to wit . 
 Wilt thou begrudge it if I must need go fetch these , and bring they 
 to the land where thou dwellest , through whatever peril we may have 
 to face ? 

 dear art thou , she say , and my very friend , but tell I : how sorry 
 wouldst thou be to leave thine own land and follow after I for the 
 sake of one who be neither thine own true love nor of thy kindred ? 
 say he : not so sorry that I should grudge against thee thereafter . 
 moreover if that much of sorrow come to I , I should deem it not ill , 
 lest I grow so over - happy that the luck rise up against I and undo 
 I . 

 she say , smile on he kindly : meseem that I be over - happy , 
 whereas I have such dear cherishing of noble friend . but now I will 
 tell thee all , and maybe thou wilt love I the less for the telling . 
 in these wood here , and lady and mistress of they , dwelleth one who 
 be not of the race of Adam . and she help and cherish I and give 
 me wisdom when I be torment and accurse , and she it be who save 
 I from the evil witch , and give I the good hap to meet your love 
 and to fetch you to their helping ; and twice hath she save I from 
 mortal peril otherwise . and she hath find I my love , thy brother 
 Arthur , and deliver he from unwit and wanhope ; and she it be who 
 draw all you hither unto we , and who deliver you from the felon 
 who have master you . and I have swear unto she that I would never 
 wholly sunder I from she ; and how shall I break mine oath and grieve 
 she , even have I the will thereto , as God wot I have not ? and she 
 weep therewith . 

 but Hugh kiss she and say : Birdalone , my dear , why weepest thou ? 
 didst thou not hear my word , that thy people should be my people , and 
 thy land my land , and that whither thou goest I will go ? dost thou 
 not trow I then ? or how deem thou I may tear thy friend Viridis 
 from thee , when she hath just find thee ? but tell I , hast thou in 
 thy mind any dwelling - place other than this ? 

 Yea , she say : I may not depart very far from this forest of 
 Evilshaw lest I grieve my wisdom - mother overmuch . but if one go 
 westward through the wood , he shall happen at last , when he cometh 
 forth of it , on a good town hight Utterhay , which lieth on the very 
 edge thereof . there be I bear , and there also I look to find three 
 dear and trusty friend to whom I owe return of their much kindness . 
 it be a noble town in a pleasant land , and thou and my lord Arthur 
 may well win both honour and worship and lordship there . and wholly 
 I trust in thy word that thou wilt not grudge against I for drag 
 thee thither . 

 Therewith she give he her hand , smile on he , though there be yet 
 trouble in her face . but he take the hand and hold it , and laugh 
 merrily and say : lo now ! how good it be for friend to take counsel 
 together ! what well may we do than go with thee thither ? and how 
 greatly will Viridis rejoice when she heareth of this . now will I go 
 and tell she and the other . 

 go then , dear lad , she say ; but as to the matter of thy fetch thy 
 child and livelihood hither , that may be not so hard nor so 
 perilous as thou deem ; and thou shalt go about it whenso thou 
 wilt , and the soon the well , and we shall abide thee here as long 
 as need may be . and therewith he go his way to tell Viridis and 
 the other of this rede which they have come to between they . 



 CHAPTER II . BIRDALONE taketh counsel with her wood - MOTHER concern 
 the matter of SIR HUGH 



 on that same day go Birdalone to the Oak of Tryst and call she 
 wood - mother to she , and she come glad and smile , and kiss and 
 embrace Birdalone , and say unto she : now I see that thou art well 
 content with this last matter I have do for thee , whereas thou art 
 come to crave a new gift of I . how know thou that ? say 
 Birdalone , laugh . say Habundia : 

 wouldst thou have come to I so soon otherwise from out of all that 
 happiness ? I have come to tell thee of my rede , say Birdalone , and 
 to ask thee if thou art like - minded with I thereon . say the wood- 
 wife : and what be thy rede , my child ? wood - mother , say Birdalone , 
 we deem that it be good for we all to go down into Utterhay where I 
 be bear , and to take up our abode therein . 

 say the wood - wife : this rede I praise , and even so would I have 
 counsel you to do ; but I abide to see if it should come from out 
 of thy breast , and now even so it hath do ; wherefore I understand 
 thy wisdom and rejoice in thee . and now crave thy boon , my child , 
 and thou shalt have it without fail . 

 Yea , say Birdalone , that will I , and the more that it be a simple 
 one and easy for thee to do . Thou know that Hugh the Green Knight 
 hath come with my she - friend seek we all the way from under the 
 Green Mountains , and he hath leave there good that he need must have 
 and folk whom he love ; and now he would go back thither , and fetch 
 all that away hither , and see to his matter as soon as may be . and 
 I would have thee counsel we what to do , whether to build a barque , 
 as perchance we may get it do , and sail the lake therein to the 
 Castle of the Quest or thereabout , and thence to ride to his land ; or 
 else to take thy guidance and safe - conduct through the wood , and to 
 bring his folk back the same way . 

 say the wood - wife : as to the way by water , I may help you little 
 therein , and meseemeth that way be many trap and wile and many 
 peril . wherefore I bid you try it not , but let the Green Knight 
 come up hither to this tree to - morrow before noon , all horse and 
 armed and array , and there shall he find three man arm in green 
 gear , horse well , and lead two sumpt - beast with they ; and they 
 shall be his until he giveth they back unto I . but if he doubteth 
 any thing betwixt the wood 's end and under the Green Mountains , let 
 he wage what folk he will besides , for these my man will have money 
 enough of his with they . but by no mean let he send they away till 
 he hath do with the wood altogether , both betwixt here and the 
 western dwelt - land , and here and Utterhay , save thou be with he . 
 but while these be with he , both he and whatsoever money he bringeth 
 shall be sure from all peril while they be in the wood . now , my 
 child , be not this the boon thou camest up hither to ask of I ? 

 yea verily , say Birdalone ; yet also I come up hither to praise thee 
 and thank thee and love thee . and she throw herself into Habundia 's 
 arm and kiss and caress she , and Habundia she in like wise . 

 spake the wood - wife : thou art the beloved child of my wisdom ; and 
 now I see of thee that thou wilt be faithful and true and love unto 
 I unto the end . and I think I can see that thou and thy man shall 
 do well and happily in Utterhay ; and the Green Knight also and thy 
 she - friend . and whatsoever thou wilt of I that I may do for thee 
 or thy friend , ask it freely , and freely shalt thou have it . but 
 this I will bid thee , that the while the Green Knight shall be go 
 about his matter , thou shalt come hither to I often ; and thy friend 
 also thou shalt bring to I , that I may see they and talk to they and 
 love they . and specially shalt thou bid Atra unto I ; for meseem 
 she be so wise already that I may learn she more wisdom , and put that 
 into her heart which may solace she and make she to cease from 
 fret her own heart , and from grief and long overmuch . and I 
 be fain to reward she in that she hath forborne to grudge against 
 thee and to bear thee enmity . for I know , my child , not from mine 
 own heart , but from the wisdom I have learn , how hardly the 
 child of Adam may bear to have that which they love take away 
 from they by another , even if they themselves might in the long last 
 have weary of it and cast it away their own self . go now , my 
 child , and do thy friend to wit what I will do for he . 

 Therewith they part , and Birdalone fare home to the house , and 
 find the fellowship of they all sit by the brookside , and 
 talk sweetly together in all joy and hope of what their life 
 should be in the new land whereto Birdalone would lead they . 
 Straightway then she tell they of Hugh and his journey , and how well 
 he should be guard in the wood both come and go . and they 
 think that right good , and they thank she and praise she , and 
 take she into their talk , and she sit down by they happily . 



 CHAPTER III . of the journeying through the forest of EVILSHAW unto 
 the town of UTTERHAY 



 on the morrow in due time Birdalone , go afoot , lead Sir Hugh , all- 
 armed and horse , to the Oak of Tryst , and there they find the three 
 man - at - arm , well - weapone and in green weed , abide they . they do 
 obeisance to Sir Hugh , and he greet they , and then without more ado 
 he kiss Birdalone and go his way with his way - leader , but 
 birdalone turn back to the house and her friend . 

 next day Birdalone bring she three she - friend unto the Trysting 
 Oak , and show they to the wood - mother , and she be kind and soft 
 with they ; and both Aurea and Viridis be shy with she , and as if 
 they fear she , but Atra be frank and free , and spake boldly . and 
 thereafter when Birdalone go to meet her wood - mother , Atra would go 
 with she if she be ask , and at last would go alone , when she 
 find that Habundia be fain of she come , so that there be not 
 many day when they meet not ; and the wood - wife fall to learn she 
 the lore of the earth , as she have do aforetime with Birdalone ; and 
 Atra wax ruddier and merry of countenance , whereof be birdalone 
 right glad , and Arthur yet more glad , and the other well content . 

 so wear the time till Hugh have be go for twenty and three day , 
 and as they walk the meadow anigh the house about undern , they see 
 a knight rid down the bent toward they , and presently they know 
 he for Hugh , and turn and hasten to meet he , so that he be 
 straightway amidst they , and on foot . dear then be the greeting 
 and caress betwixt they , and when it be over , and Birdalone have 
 lead away his horse and dight it for he , and have get he victual 
 and drink , and they be all sit on the grass together , he tell 
 they how he have fare . he have do all his matter in the Land under 
 the Green Mountains , and have give over his land and house to a man 
 of his lineage , his cousin , a good knight , and have take from he of 
 gold and good what he would . then he have take his two bairn and 
 their nurse , and an old squire and five sergeant , whereof one be 
 his foster - brother , and the other man somewhat stricken in year , 
 and have depart with they . sithence he have come his way to 
 Greenford , and have hold talk therein with the prior of a great and 
 fair house of Black Canons , and have give he no little wealth 
 wherewith to re - do the Castle of the Quest what be need , and for 
 livelihood of four canon to dwell there , and Leonard to be their 
 prior , that there they might remember Sir Baudoin their dear friend 
 daily in the office , and do good unto his soul . sithence he have 
 ride to the Castle of the Quest with the say Prior of St. Austin 
 of Greenford , and have find Leonard , and have settle all the business 
 how it be to be do . thereafter he have return to Greenford , and 
 gather his folk , and get he go , under the guidance of Habundia 's 
 folk , by castle and thorp and town the near way to the edge of 
 Evilshaw . and they have come to the forest , and ride it six day 
 without mishap ; and when they have come to the Oak of Tryst once more , 
 the way - leader say that it be well if all they together tarry 
 not much long in the forest ; wherefore they have bring they to a 
 fair wood - lawn , and there they encamp , and be there as now . and , 
 say Hugh , there be they abide I , and it be in my mind that this 
 very eve we go , all of we , and meet they there , if ye may truss your 
 good in that while ; but as to victual , we have plenty , and it 
 needeth not . and then to - morrow shall we wend our way as straight as 
 may be toward the good town of Utterhay . 

 all they yeasaid it , though in her heart maybe Birdalone have be 
 fain of abide a little long in her own land ; but she spake no 
 word thereof . and they all set to work to the trussing up of their 
 good , and then turn their back on the Great Water , and come up 
 into the woodland , and so to the camp in the wood - lawn . and there 
 have Viridis a joyful meeting with her babe , and she gladden the 
 heart of Sir Hugh 's man - at - arm by her kind greeting ; and they 
 rejoice in meet Aurea and Atra again , and they wonder at 
 Birdalone and her beauty , and their heart go out to she , both the 
 old man 's and the young one . but Habundia 's man look on it all 
 like image of warrior . 

 there then they feast merrily that evening . but when the morrow 
 be come they be speedily on the way toward Utterhay ; and the way- 
 leader guide they so well and wisely , that by noon of the fifth day 
 they be come forth of the wood and on to the bent that look down 
 upon the town of Utterhay . there turn to Hugh the three way- 
 leader , and spake : Lord , we have do thee the service which we 
 be bid ; if thou hast no further need of we , give we leave . 

 say Hugh : leave ye have , and I shall give you a great reward ere ye 
 go . say the chief of they : Nay , lord , no reward may we take , save 
 a token from thee that thou art content with we . what token shall it 
 be ? say Hugh . Quoth the way - leader : that each of we kiss the Lady 
 birdalone on the mouth , for she it be that be verily our mistress 
 under our great mistress . 

 laugh Hugh thereat , but the man laugh not ; then spake Hugh : this 
 must be at the lady 's own will . even so , say they . 

 then Hugh bring Birdalone thither and tell she what be toward , and 
 she consent to the kiss with a good will , and say to each of the 
 man after they have kiss she : Herewith goeth my love to the 
 mistress and queen of the wood ; do ye bear the same unto she . and 
 thereafter those way - leader fare back into the wood . 

 now they gather themselves together and go down toward Utterhay , and 
 make a brave show , what with the sumpt - horse , and the goodly array 
 of the four lady , and the glitter war - gear of the man - at - arm ; 
 and Sir Hugh and Sir Arthur display their pennon as they go . 

 all this see the warder on the wall of Utterhay ; and they tell the 
 captain of the porte , and he come up on to the wall , and a man with 
 he ; and when he see this bright company come forth from the wood , 
 he bid man to he , two score of they , all weapone , and he do on 
 his armour , and ride out - a - gate with they to meet those new - comer ; 
 and this he do , not because he do not see they to be but few , but 
 because they come forth out of Evilshaw , and then doubt if they 
 be trustworthy . 

 so he meet they two bowshot from the gate , and ride forward till he 
 be close to the wayfarer ; and when he behold the loveliness of the 
 woman , and especially of Birdalone , who wear that day the gleaming- 
 glitter gown which Habundia have give she , he be abash , and 
 deem yet more that he have to do with folk of the Faery . but he 
 spake courteously , and say , turn to Hugh , who ride the foremost : 
 Fair sir , would ye tell unto the man whose business it be to 
 safeguard the good town of Utterhay what folk ye be , and on what 
 errand ye ride , and how it be that ye come forth from Evilshaw safe , 
 in good case , with pennon display , as if the say wood be your 
 very own livelihood ? for , sooth to say , hitherto we have find this , 
 that all man dread Evilshaw , and none will enter it uncompelle . 

 Thereto answer Hugh : I hight Sir Hugh the Green Knight , and be 
 come from under the Green Mountain ; and this be Sir Arthur , call 
 the Black Squire , but a knight he be verily , and of great kindre and 
 a warrior most doughty . and he hath be captain of the good town of 
 Greenford west away through the wood yonder a long way , and hath do 
 the town and the frank thereof mickle good service in scatter and 
 destroy the evil company of the Red Hold , which hold we take by 
 force of arm from the felon who hold it for the torment and plague 
 of the country - side . 

 now as to our errand , we be minded to dwell in your good town of 
 Utterhay , and take our part with your folk , and we have wealth enow 
 thereto , so as to be beholden to none ; and as time go on we may 
 serve you in diver wise , and not least in this maybe , that with a 
 good will we shall draw sword for your peace and the freedom of they 
 of Utterhay . 

 when the captain hear these word , he make obeisance to Sir Hugh , 
 and say : Fair sir , though we be here a long way from Greenford , yet 
 have we hear some tale of the deed of you , and surely the porte and 
 all the folk shall be fain of your corning . yet I pray thee be not 
 wrath ; for there be a custom of the good town , that none may enter 
 its gate come from out of this Forest of Evilshaw , save he leave 
 some pledge or caution with I , be it his wealth , or the body of some 
 friend or fellow , or , if nought else , his very own body . wherefore 
 if thou , Sir Green Knight , wilt but give we some sure pledge , then 
 will I turn about and ride with you back and through the gate into 
 Utterhay ; and doubtless , when the mayor hath see you and speak with 
 you , the say pledge shall be render to you again . 

 Ere Hugh might answer , come Birdalone forth and say : Sir captain , 
 if I , who be the lady of the Black Squire here , be hostage good 
 enough , then take I , and if need be , chain I to make surer of I . 
 and she draw near unto he smile , and hold out her hand as if for 
 the manacle . 

 but when the captain see she thus , all the blood stir in his body 
 for joy of her beauty , and he might but just sit his horse for his 
 wonder and longing ; but he say : the saint forbid it , lady , that I 
 should do thee any hurt or displeasure , or aught save the most 
 worship I may . but thy hostage I will take , Sir Knight if thou be 
 content to yield she , whereas in an hour belike she shall be free 
 again . and now fare we all gateward again . 

 so then they all ride on together , birdalone by the captain 's left 
 hand ; and as they pass by the poor house without the wall , she 
 look and see the one which have be her mother 's dwelling , so oft 
 and so closely have she tell she all about it . 

 thus then they enter Utterhay , and the captain lead they straight to 
 the mote - house whereas the mayor and the porte be sit ; and much 
 people follow they through the street , wonder at they , and 
 praise the loveliness of the woman , and the frank and gallant 
 bearing of the man - at - arm . 

 so they light down at the mote - house and be bring to the mayor , 
 and when he have speak they but a little , and have come to himself 
 again from the fear and abashment that he have of they , he show 
 himself full fain of their come , and bid they welcome to the good 
 town , and take they into his own house to gueste , until folk might 
 dight a very goodly house which the porte do give unto they . 

 but some two hour afterwards , when they be house in all content , 
 as they sit in the hall of the mayor , which be great and goodly , 
 talk and devise with worthy of Utterhay , there enter two 
 fair and frank - looking young man , who go straight up to Birdalone , 
 and the first knelt down before she and kiss her hand , and say : O 
 our lady , and art thou verily come to we ! o our happiness and the 
 joy of this day ! 

 but when she see he and hear he and feel the touch of his hand , 
 she bend down to he and kiss he on the forehead , for she know he 
 that it be Robert Gerardson . 

 then the other man come up to she as if he also would have kneel to 
 she , but his purpose change , and he cast his arm about her body and 
 fall to kiss her face all over , weep the while , and then he 
 draw off and stand tremble before she and she , all blush like a 
 red rise and laugh a little , and yet with the tear in her eye , 
 say : o Giles Gerardson , and thou , Robert , how fain I be to see you 
 twain ; but tell I , be your father well ? yea , verily , our dear lady , 
 say Robert , and it will be unto he as a fresh draught of youth when 
 he wotteth that thou art come to dwell amongst we ; for so it be , O 
 lady belove , be it not ? say he . yea , forsooth , or even so I hope , 
 say Birdalone . but here be other friend that ye must need know , 
 if we come to dwell together here in peace ; and then go and fetch I 
 hither your father . 

 Therewith she present they unto Arthur and Hugh and the three 
 lady of the Quest , and all they greet they kindly and in all 
 honour ; and the Gerardsons love and worship they , and especially 
 the lovely lady , the she - friend of their lady . 

 and while they be about this , in cometh old Gerard himself , and 
 when Birdalone see he at the door , she arise and run to meet he , 
 and cast her arm about he as if she be his own daughter ; and most 
 joyful be the meeting betwixt they . 



 CHAPTER IV . of the abiding in UTTERHAY in LOVE and CONTENTMENT 



 now when seven day be wear , the mayor make a great feast at his 
 house , and thither be bid all the man of the porte and other 
 worthy , and great merchant who have come into their town ; and the 
 say feast be give in honour of these new - comer , and that day they 
 sit on the dai , and all the guest worship they and wonder at 
 their beauty ; and nought be speak of for many day save the glory 
 and hope that there be in this lovely folk . 

 but the next day after the feast be they bring to their house in 
 all triumph ; and it be as fair as might be think of , and there 
 they dwelt a while in rest and peace , and great recourse there be 
 there of Gerard and his son . 

 but ere the winter be over , be Hugh and Arthur and Gerard and his 
 son take to the freedom of Utterhay ; and thereafter spake the chief 
 man of the porte and the master of the craft unto the two knight 
 by the mouth of the mayor ; and he tell they , what already they partly 
 know , that the good town have of late get many enemy , whereas it 
 be wealthy and not very strong , and that now two such warrior 
 have come amongst they , they be minded to strengthen themselves , 
 if only they two would of their gentleness and meekness become their 
 war - duke to lead they against the foeman . but the two friend 
 answer that it be well their will to dwell there neighbourly , and 
 do they all the help they might , and that they would not gainsay the 
 worship they offer they nor the work that should go with it . 

 with that answer be all man well content and more : and then the 
 mayor say that the mind of the porte it be to strengthen the wall 
 and the gate , and to build a good and fair castle , meet for any 
 earl , join on to the wall by the face that look west , that be to 
 say , on to Evilshaw ; and that like the war - duke well . 

 so when spring come it be set about , but it be five year adoe , 
 and before it be all finish the war - duke enter into it , and 
 dwelt there with their wife and their friend in all honour . and a 
 little thereafter , whether they would or no , the man of Utterhay have 
 to handle weapon and fare afield to meet the foe with the valiant 
 man of the craft , and what of wag man they might get . and well 
 and valiantly be they lead by their duke , and they come to their 
 above , and gain both wealth and honour thereby ; and from that time 
 forward begin the increase of Utterhay under those two captain , who 
 be unto they as in old time the consul have be unto the roman 
 folk , save that they change they not year by year as the Romans be 
 will not . 

 so wear the day , and all those friend dwelt together in harmony and 
 joy ; though the wearing of time work change amongst they . for 
 Robert Gerardson begin in no long while to look on Aurea with eye of 
 love ; and at last he come to Birdalone and crave her leave to woo 
 the say lady , and she grant it with a good will , and be fain 
 thereof , whereas she see that Aurea sorely lack a mate ; and scarce 
 might she have a well than be Robert ; so in process of time they 
 two be wed and dwelt together happily . 

 Forsooth Birdalone have be fainer yet might she have see Giles 
 Gerardson and Atra draw together . but though they be dear friend 
 and there be much converse betwixt they , this betid not , so far as 
 we have hear . 

 the old Gerard dwelt happily amongst they all for fifteen year after 
 they have come to Utterhay , and then fall asleep , a very old man . 

 as to the wood of Evilshaw , it be not once a year only that 
 Birdalone and Arthur seek thither and meet the wood - mother , but a 
 half - score of time or more , might be , in the year 's circle ; and ever 
 be she kind and love with they , and they with she . 

 but of all those fellow it be Atra that have long dealing with 
 the wood - wife ; for while would she leave Utterhay and her friend 
 and fare lonesome up into Evilshaw , and find Habundia and abide with 
 she in all kindness holden for a month or more . and ever a little 
 before these departure betid would she fall moody and few - speak , 
 but she come back ever from the wood calm and kind and well - liking . 
 amidst all these coming and going somewhat wear off the terror of 
 Evilshaw ; yet never be it account other than a daring deed to 
 enter it alone without fellowship ; and most have liefer that some man 
 of religion be of their company therein , or they would bear about 
 they something holy or bless to hold the evil thing . 

 now when all this hath be say , we have no more to tell about this 
 company of friend , the most of whom have once haunt the land about 
 the Water of the Wondrous Isles , save that their love never sunder , 
 and that they live without shame and die without fear . so here be 
 an end .
